  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2e8482af-b469-4780-90b1-08534cca2c19'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText2887922006234881689" style="display:none"><b>Life as the Preliator is harder than Ellie ever imagined.</b><br />Balancing real life with the responsibility of being Heaven’s warrior is a challenge for Ellie. Her relationship with Will has become all business, though they both long for each other. And now that the secret of who she really is has come out, so have Hell’s strongest reapers. Grown bold and more vicious, the demonic threaten her in the light of day and stalk her in the night.<br /><br /><b>She’s been warned.</b><br />Cadan, a demonic reaper, comes to her with information about Bastian’s new plan to destroy Ellie’s soul and use an ancient relic to wake all the souls of the damned and unleash them upon humanity. As she fights to stay ahead of Bastian’s schemes , the revelations about those closest to her awaken a dark power within Ellie that threatens to destroy everything—including herself.<br /><br /><b>She’ll be betrayed.</b><br />Treachery comes even from those whom she loves, and Ellie is broken by the deaths of those who stood beside her in this Heavenly war. Still, she must find a way to save the world, herself, and her love for Will. If she fails, there will be hell to pay.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clarté" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clarté" href="/user/show/6801597-clart">Clarté</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231993585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7234677476732015434"><b>
  <i>SPOILERS BELOW</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>
  <i>You've been warned</i>
</i><br/><br/><i> Oh, and sorry for the bad language in advance! </i><br/><br/>First of all, let me get one thing straight. This book was <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713796.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713797.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I know, it's not the newest book in the stores, but I got my signed copy *proud* last week, and you know <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713798.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>for waiting for it. <br/>And it's over <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713799.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>but I'm writing this anyway.<br/><br/>So, in the beginning, I mean in the very beginning all that sexual tension was bearable. Really. But then when the room was getting hotter Ava had to arrive and freeze everything. No, n</span>
  <span id="freeText7234677476732015434" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>SPOILERS BELOW</i>
</b><br><br><br><i>
  <i>You've been warned</i>
</i><br><br><i> Oh, and sorry for the bad language in advance! </i><br><br>First of all, let me get one thing straight. This book was <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713796.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713797.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I know, it's not the newest book in the stores, but I got my signed copy *proud* last week, and you know <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>for waiting for it. <br>And it's over <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713799.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>but I'm writing this anyway.<br><br>So, in the beginning, I mean in the very beginning all that sexual tension was bearable. Really. But then when the room was getting hotter Ava had to arrive and freeze everything. No, not because she is so cool, but because she is so totally frigid that even thinking about her makes my teeth chatter, so I was like<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362624i/713800.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I remind you, this was in the beginning. As the story went on, things changed. Right, what a surprise, I'm so smart for writing such a statement. Whatever. So as we went on, my hatered toward her diminished. No, I'm not saying I grew to like her, but I don't have any problems with her and I'm not thinking <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713801.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> when she is on. <br><br>Sorry for the random order, but now come the sad parts of the wonder that Courtney gave us, and yes, by wonder I mean her novel. I know there wasn't really an important character to die in <i>Angelfire</i> - yes, you know Ragnuk wasn't all that important regarding everything what's going on here - but really, was this necessary? Our dear author killed 2 kind-of-main characters, plus one who was just sweet to have, so I'm telling you <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713802.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>First Ellie's mom died <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713803.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I could handle that, I'm tough. But then came Nathaniel and it broke my heart into tiny shards and as Will lost his head Courtney was just stomping on the pieces until only dust was left of my dearest organ. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713804.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>When Bastian died... Well I can't just say to <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713805.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>but... I don't know. I know I should have been kind of happy that the enemy died, but I was more sad than content, to be frank. <br><br>Oh yeah, one thing I gotta say. Either I'm so freaking smart, or I don't know, but <i>how the Hell</i> did I figure out that <b>a)</b> Cadan was Bastian's son and <b>b)</b> so was Will? Because I don't think it was that obvious. I know Courtney wanted it to be so extremely surprising, and yeah, if she'd dropped that bomb in the previous book, then I would have been surprised, but here... Nope. Call it women's intuition or whatever you'd like, but after the first time Cadan was involved, I would have bet he was Bastian's son. And around the half of the book, when Bastian was on the spot, and I went to bed to sleep, I was thinking about the last chapter I'd read, and the Will-part just popped into my head in that <i>"what if...</i> sort of way. I wasn't even totally serious as I think I was half asleep already, but maybe that was the key to solve it. And when Bastian revealed the truth, I was laughing in myself, because he just proved what a smartass I am. So yeah, it was good the way it was written, I'm just delusional. Though I really would have appreciated it if Ellie had told Will the truth. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362624i/713806.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now we arrived to the part where pink ponies neigh lullabies and uhh <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347860ra/702209.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Just quickly. Ellie is the character who is standing the closest to me. No, I don't mean in the book, I mean in literature on average. She is almost perfectly like me, except for some tiny details including that I'm not some kind of super warrior kicking reapers' asses and I don't have an unbelievably pefect Guardian, which is kind of fortunate considering that I would have to carry a bucket all day long to drool into. But she makes the decisions I would, she always changes her mind about things like I do, <b>and!</b> she didn't let Cadan kiss her, and I'm so so so SO grateful for that Courtney that you didn't make them kiss <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/264612.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Because that would have been just <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347471ra/701853.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and totally cliché.<br><br>Oh and last but not least, Will <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713807.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I swear Will's were the most difficult parts to read. Why? Because I was constantly getting my hands burned by the steaming hotness coming from the pages and wondering <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713808.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously. That sexuality was overwhelming. And he doesn't even know about it. I mean how freaking perfect and sexy that is? Pulling it off just like that? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713809.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And when things are about to turn really really interesting Ellie turns him down. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380361846ra/712898.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>If Will was horny and wanted to sleep with me<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713810.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713811.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713812.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713813.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So you see, I wouldn't want to wait for anything... Unfortunately I'm not Ellie, so these things are just in my imagination and sweet dreams <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362624i/713814._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But let me also express you how cute he is and even though sometimes I feel like he should be less perfect, it's just good this way I guess, because he doesn't make me believe that such guys exist in our world, so <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/397125.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>instead of the cruel reality.<br>But then... One thing I really didn't expect <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713815.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>I knew something would happen because it was the calm time before storm, but <i>THIS</i>??? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/319715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That reaper <b>
  <i>bit</i>
</b> him!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713816.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And now he is dying <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362624ra/713817.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And they only have one week to save him<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362625ra/713818.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And something tells me they will only be able to do so in the very last moment. Because he cannot die. That's <b>
  <i>impossible.</i>
</b> I would be<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362625ra/713819.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>in a moment. And Cadan has to be the one to help? Why do I have such a bad feeling about this one? If he puts his things anywhere near Ellie... <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362625ra/713820.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But all in all, WotW can join my shelf of favourites of course, because it was freaking awesome! Thank you Courtney! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362625i/713821.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_207428448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207428448" />
    <a title="Lyndsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey"><img alt="Lyndsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288890060p2/4224396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207428448?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-4-stars">reviewed-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=pov-primarily-female">pov-primarily-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=1st-person">1st-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-angels-fallen-etc">about-angels-fallen-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-super-special-chosen-one">about-super-special-chosen-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=series-2nd-book">series-2nd-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207428448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1577721196136471229"> <br/>Hah. <b>More like Wangst of the Wicked!</b> I kid, I kid.<br/><br/>I made a comment about the first book being Buffy Season One: Disney Channel Version. Well, the sequel jumped straight into Buffy Season Six territory. <u>It's dark, sexy, and witty</u>. Much more so than the first.<br/><br/>Admittedly, I wasn't too impressed with Angelfire, the first book in this series, but Wings of the Wicked is abundantly more fun than it's predecessor.<br/><br/>The characters are starting to get into a comfort zone with each other and the chemistry b</span>
  <span id="freeText1577721196136471229" style="display:none"> <br />Hah. <b>More like Wangst of the Wicked!</b> I kid, I kid.<br /><br />I made a comment about the first book being Buffy Season One: Disney Channel Version. Well, the sequel jumped straight into Buffy Season Six territory. <u>It's dark, sexy, and witty</u>. Much more so than the first.<br /><br />Admittedly, I wasn't too impressed with Angelfire, the first book in this series, but Wings of the Wicked is abundantly more fun than it's predecessor.<br /><br />The characters are starting to get into a comfort zone with each other and the chemistry between them is coming alive. The straight forward no-frills prose carries you right into the action and drama.      <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Rundown</u>
</b><br /><br />With the help of her guardian Will, Ellie battles the forces of darkness. She is the Preliator, the only one in the world who wields awesome reaper-slaying, sickle-shaped swords that are infused with the heavenly flame of Angelfire, and she's getting even better in battle. Things have gotten complicated with angelic Will, and he and Ellie fight the feelings they have for each other. A demonic reaper named Cadan begins to make advances toward Ellie, but can she trust him?  Now a strong force of darkness is rising up and it will take everything the Preliator and her friends have got to face this new evil.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Characterization and Romance</b>
</u><br /><br />In the first book, even though it's written in first person, I never felt like I was getting to know Ellie because of her Mary Sue tendencies. Yet somehow, I've really grown to care about her in the sequel, as have many of the other characters. <b>There is Love Triangle.</b> I know what you're thinking: Noooooooooooooooo! Or maybe: Yes, yes, YES! But I actually really liked both of the boys. <br /><br /><u>First, there's Will.</u> (Why does every book have a Will these days?) His mouth says, "I love you but I can't be with you." But his eyes say, "I can't stay away."<br /><br /><u>Then there's Cadan.</u> His mouth says, "I love you whether or not want to be with me." But his eyes say, "I'm gonna lock you <i>in my basement</i>."<br /><br />Guess which one she goes for? NOT the creepy stalker guy. Oh wait, they're both kind of stalkers. Well, they call themselves "guardians" or "protectors" but we all know what that means. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[PEDOSUPERNATURALS! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kidding .<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's not at all weird that they are a thousand and she is seventeen. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />One thing I appreciated: Ellie considers having sex before marriage. Gasp!! Blasphemy! As long as no one puts a fanged supernatural baby in her, I'm fine with it. And PHEW! There were some <u>hot</u> scenes. Ellie was much less <i>chaste</i> and she liked it!<br /><br />Shockingly, this book took a turn for dark. Several important characters are lost. And man... The characters in this book truly know how to grieve. It's not at all like other similar YA books where close friends or family members die and no one seems to care. So many intense moments of pain and rage fill these pages. They scream, they cry, they bawl their eyes out. Their agony is so believable in those moments.<br /><br />The characterization is infinitely better in this book. I looked forward to the exchanges between Ellie and almost everyone this time around. Whereas the first book was mainly Ellie being confused and asking questions and being all "Woe is me," our heroine really came into her own in Wings of the Wicked. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>The World-Building</b>
</u> <br /><br />This book threw in even more aspects of Buffydom, namely patrolling, which was not an aspect of the first book due to the whole "getting to know you" phase that Ellie was going through with Will and the new world unfolding around her. Patrols were always a important part of the storylines in Buffy, but I had mixed feelings about them being brought into the Angelfire series. Don't the two share quite a bit of similarities as it is? It makes me wonder what's next: turning Ellie's bestie, Kate, into an evil black-eyed witch lesbian?<br /><br />Still - I have to admit that I ended up enjoying seeing the patrols included. It brought a sense of familiarity to it, complemented by the fact that the characters began to vibe with each other so well in battle. <br /><br />Despite the obvious similarities to other series, the world was intense and more evolved this time around. They delve a bit deeper into Ellie's past and the specifics around it, but still left a lot to be learned in the upcoming books.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>The Verdict</b>
</u> <br /><br />The plotline revolves strongly around action and romance and seems to be setting up for tons of love triangle tension in the next book, which I am greatly looking forward to.  Though the writing is  "filled to the brim" with cliche, it didn't matter. I found myself reading compulsively with a stupid grin on my face the whole time.<br /><br />If you're a fan of angel mythology and looking for that next thing, this series just might be it! If you read the first book and are unsure about continuing, let me assure you that I greatly enjoyed it and did not regret it for one second.<br /><br />As much as I liked this one, I still can't give it five stars, mainly because of an excess of cheesy lines and cliche. However, <u>I enjoyed this one exponentially more than the first book</u>. In fact, I wouldn't have believed how much better it is if I hadn't read it with my own two eyes.<br /><br />Much less Seventh Heaven (<i>When I see their happy faces smiling back at me-eeee.</i> Yep, now it's going to be stuck in your head. Bwuahahahaha!) and much more Buffy and Supernatural. Really. It was like watching some sort of bizarre crossover spin-off of the two shows and I LOVED it.   </span>
  <a data-text-id="1577721196136471229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=angels-and-demons">angels-and-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=awesome-heroine">awesome-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=awesome-ya">awesome-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer257110939&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257110939" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5149256634598984186"><b>Actual final rating: 4.5 stars. But I rounded up. Because it lost half a star on a technicality only.</b><br/><br/>So the other night I had this dream.<br/><br/>It was the beginning of the new high school year after graduation. Me and my graduating class were chilling in this weird white room that looked kind of like the lunch rooms in <i>Cellblock 6: Female Lock Up</i> and watching, through a set of Perspex windows looking out into the front hall, as the new Grade 12 kids march in to their uncertain fate.<br/><br/>This guy I know (he </span>
  <span id="freeText5149256634598984186" style="display:none"><b>Actual final rating: 4.5 stars. But I rounded up. Because it lost half a star on a technicality only.</b><br /><br />So the other night I had this dream.<br /><br />It was the beginning of the new high school year after graduation. Me and my graduating class were chilling in this weird white room that looked kind of like the lunch rooms in <i>Cellblock 6: Female Lock Up</i> and watching, through a set of Perspex windows looking out into the front hall, as the new Grade 12 kids march in to their uncertain fate.<br /><br />This guy I know (he graduated at the same time as me. Why was he returning in my dream? Dafuq?) was one of those people walking in for the new year. I actually lol'd in my dream because he randomly lost his footing when he was walking down the hall and spontaneously smashed his face off the display case, but he was fine, no harm, no foul. <br /><br />After a while we get bored of this, and head to some kind of weird cafeteria after-party where everyone from my old school in the UK is there too. Across the lunch room I lock eyes with this guy I was totes in love with when I was like fifteen and OMG! It's like a fairytale with Roma Pizza and inappropriate Happy Birthday! napkins. <br /><br />Gaiz, srsly. I have absolutely no idea why this guy appeared in my dream. Sure, when I was fifteen it was deep and it was real. I went there: I really did. I wrote his name in all of my notebooks and tore girls' hair out to get the seat behind him in class so I could talk to him and fuck, I was all on imagining what our wedding would be like.<br /><br />Hopefully, you can all appreciate the growth and change I've thankfully gone through since the days of yore.<br /><br />But I left for Canada, and I've had no contact with the guy for literally years. I haven't thought about him for a long, <i>long</i> time. And then suddenly he pops up in the dreamscape lunchroom. What's a girl to do?<br /><br />So we get all cozy and he kisses my forehead like Edward Cullen. Naturally, I get distracted by the nearby hotdog stand, which is basically a fish tank full of hotdog buns. Where's the meat, I ask? Fifteen Boy points to this steel door behind me and--oh, yeah. We're suddenly outside now, and it's got that dream lighting. You know, like the lighting in <i>Sleepy Hollow</i>? This is when I realize some creepy shit is going on.<br /><br />So he takes two hotdog buns (I also take two) and heads for the steel door seemingly leading to nowhere. I go after him and we head up through this elevator to a weird compound that's round, outdoors but enclosed with a ring of high-rise stores above. Each of the stores is numbered one to thirteen. <br /><br />(I swear to SHIVA. This is not a rickroll.)<br /><br />Suddenly the guy is gone and one of my best friends (in Canada) is with me. She seems largely unimpressed, but she's like that in real life. She's the most calm, chill, easygoing Jamaican person ever. It's such bliss hanging out with her. You don't even need to make conversation. <br /><br />You just have to be.<br /><br />So anyway I figure I'd better get an actual hotdog to put in the bun. (Innuendo not intended.) There are rainforest trees all around this compound and the air is kind of humid--if any of you have ever been to the aviary in Niagara-on-the-Lake and been through that bit with all the waterfalls and the hilarious red birds with pipe cleaner legs, then you'll have a rough idea of the terrain here.<br /><br />So my friend runs off to one of the big doorways in the side of the compound (kind of like the opening into the ruins at the beginning of <i>Tomb Raider: Anniversary</i> except without the flesh-eating wolves) and I stop by the entrance, because there's this little button you need to press to make the elevator inside the walkway, up to the shops above, work. My friend waves me in and I follow her, but she gets into the elevator before I do and then I'm stuck there like a spanner with my empty hotdog buns.<br /><br />I head back out to the button. It sits like a catherine wheel, colored orange and yellow, and you have to spin it to the right number of shop you want to get to, then press the Go! button in the center.<br /><br />(I promise you guys, I am not fucking with you. This is the serious truth.)<br /><br />So I spin it to shop number four, but I'm not fast enough to get into the elevator. I have to go back and press it again, and then I leap into the elevator just in time.<br /><br />Let me explain to you what this elevator was like.<br /><br />The doors opened vertically, and were made of wire and wood. When you jumped inside, you landed at the bottom of this wet, muddy slope, and then you somehow were pushed up that slope at <i>lightning</i> speed, and there were all these trees and rocks and shit and a voice came over the intercom telling you to curl up in the fetal position to avoid hitting any of the crap on the track. <br /><br />Swear it.<br /><br />So I reach the top, and I'm literally thrown off this slope, right into the air. I'm headed for this Super-Marioesque mushroom cap, pink with yellow spots, where my friend is waiting for me. Suddenly my dog is with me, and she's being carried by this weird bug that I swear is one of the monster companions in <i>Final Fantasy XIII-2</i> and then we're dropped and we land on the mushroom cap, which is all light because it's inside this room with all these windows around it. There are a few other people there, and they all have dogs with them, but my friend is allergic to dogs so she doesn't have one. I say she can share mine.<br /><br />Even in my dreams, I'm a giving soul. <br /><br />(Lol.)<br /><br />So then all of a sudden this GI Joe guy comes blasting out of nowhere and he orders us to do this massive obstacle course before we can get our tiny insignificant fucking hotdog. Like, what the fuck? It's a fucking hotdog, not a Nobel Prize. I just wanted my hotdog, dammit!<br /><br />Anyway, we have to do the obstacle course riding on our dogs' backs like horses. My dog is relatively small (she's a spaniel) but somehow I managed to get upon my steed and we start the obstacle course, which is kind of like those challenges you have to do in <i>Super Mario Sunshine</i> if you go through the green pipe looking for a cheat of a Shine Sprite.<br /><br />So anyway, me and my dog NAIL it and we win. We veer off course a little because it's like playing a video game, with controls like the fucking painful ones you have to grapple with when you're on the hang-glider in <i>Assassin's Creed: Revelations</i> getting pulled along by Sophia. Anyway, we win, and then tra-la-la!<br /><br />The dream is over. <br /><br />And I never got my hotdog. <br /><br /><i>Wings of the Wicked</i> is just like my dream. No, it's not about Ellie's tormented quest for a hotdog, but it is about a whole lot of weird, scary, colorful and bizarre happenings that somehow, for some reason, come together to make sense.<br /><br />Let me explain.<br /><br />Like my dream, <i>Wings</i> leaps into the plot from the very first chapter. I went straight for the hotdogs; Ellie goes straight for the reapers. And it was this that I appreciated. Any of you who know me are probably aware that <i>Angelfire</i> is definitely not my favorite book in the world for two staple reasons: Ellie, and the writing.<br /><br />In <i>Wings</i>, Ellie grows from a little sapling that can be annihilated by one peck from a chicken to a sword-wielding foxglove (foxgloves can stop your heart with their poison. DON'T GO NEAR THEM. DON'T!). Where as the Ellie from the first book would make a joke of her duties, this Ellie is absolutely serious about them. She still takes time out for partying and homework and shit, but a wake-up call is all it takes for her to realize that shit just got real, and you have to stop giggling when something tries to gut you with their fingernail.<br /><br />Will gained a little more favor with me here. I wasn't that chuffed about him in the first book either, but in <i>Wings</i> he gains a little more depth and backstory, enough for him to prism from a piece of cardboard to an actual character. I loved the revelation that he slept with Ava. It gave him this fabulous, human quality, a real weakness and a mistake from the past that negated the whole "perfect love interest" trope that's been sniffing around YA of late.<br /><br />Speaking of Ava: um, hello, Favorite Character! I fucking love this woman. She's amazing. She has so much depth and interest to her, so much so that I was desperate to find out more about her. I wanted to get inside <i>her</i> head and find out a little more about her story (which was heart-breaking, but added to her resilience). <br /><br />A pretty large portion of this book revolves around the deaths of secondary characters, and being aware that people would die before I started reading this book assured me of two things:<br /><br />(a) There is every chance in the world that these deaths will wind up being oddly funny rather than sad.<br />(b) There is every chance in the world that these deaths will make me want to die too. From grief. And lack of hotdogs.<br /><br />It was pretty much a B all round.<br /><br />Seriously, the deaths in this book took it out of me. I do feel like you have to have a certain kind of relationship in your own life to really connect with the deaths in <i>Wings</i>, and I'm one of the lucky ones. <br /><br />Let's look at this: I was reading the portion where Ellie's mom dies when we were driving along the highway, headed for some Swedish fun at IKEA. The horrific torment of reading the death scene haunted me for the rest of the day, so much so that I did the whole tourist thing and held on to my mom's bag strap all the way around the store. I did not want to let go of my mother, ever, because then a reaper would get her, and fuck, that can't happen.<br /><br />That is literally what this book did to me. It made me terrified.<br /><br />And that's <b>awesome</b>.<br /><br />Nathaniel's death was an absolute blindside. I was sobbing, yelling at the book, slapping myself, comfort eating my weight in chocolate muffins... <br /><br />Just why, Courtney? Why'd that have to happen?<br /><br />As if it wasn't enough that I was a blubbering mess, the characters in <i>Wings</i> really mourn with you. Remember Katniss when Finnick died, how she made it all about herself and then forgot about him as if "fuck, it's just a death of my friend, at least it wasn't me, because I'm the most important one!" Well, <i>Wings</i> is nothing like that. NOTHING. It's brutal. Ellie and the gang wear themselves out mourning over the friends they lose. They go crazy, they scream, they cry, they ask God why, because that's what happens when people you love die. <br /><br />This book has this honest, human, emotional aura that I couldn't shake. It was like a coming-of-age story. Trials and tribulations from a group of relatable characters. Awesome.<br /><br />The romance was the romance: sweet, cute and yes, a little sexual. I like that. There is entirely too much no-sex-before-marriage dogma in YA today, and the fact that Ellie was planning to sleep with Will after prom (it's only interrupted by Will getting poisoned and ending up on the brink of death. Shame, dat) is just...honest. It's refreshing and true and warmed me to the characters I'd previously been so detached from.<br /><br />Look. I won't say it was perfect, because it wasn't. As much as I liked the Ellie/Will dynamic in this book, I <i>really</i> wish Ellie had battled as hard as Will did. She didn't. She could have, but she didn't. I don't know why that is. I guess I felt like in battle Will was either in the way and a liability, or leading the charge. Ellie is the one with the angelfire: she is the one who ought to be heading up the war against the reapers. She was far too idle.<br /><br />The Ellie/Will partnership isn't the reason why I dropped the half-star, because it's not really a fair test of Ellie's prowess. In the first half of the book, she kicked so much ass I was cheering, so I suppose her lack of that same prowess in the second half was perhaps due to her losing her mother and Nathaniel and still being in a state of downtrodden grief. <br /><br />The technical reason why I took off half a star is that the Rule of Abeko* was broken by this book. It was broken spectacularly, and no book that breaks the Rule of Abeko can ever be a true five stars for me. That's just the way it has to be, I'm afraid. And no book is an exception. <br /><br />On the plus side, the plot and writing of this book thrilled me. The action scenes were <i>hardcore</i> awesome and the plot, which accelerates at breakneck speed with just enough time in between to sweeten the characters, made me physically tense. I also love Court's mythology. With the exception of the Rule of Abeko, her blending of Eastern religion with rather tired Judeo-Christian lore is really refreshing. What I love about this series is its unpredictability: curveballs come at you like gnats in the summertime. You heard it here, kids.<br /><br />Is there anything else I have to say? I don't think so, but I would definitely recommend this book. Even if you hated <i>Angelfire</i>, you should at least take a stab at this one. It's killer. I swear.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><i>*The "Rule of Abeko" states that Lilith is evil only because Biblical patriarchy declares her to be so. It also states that the imagery of Lilith being a baby-eater and a destroyer of virginal maidens is only in place because she must be Biblically demonized for (a) not being a baby-making machine and (b) not being meek. <br /><br />Breaking this rule would be to represent Lilith as evil, a baby-eater or a raging jealous bitch. Examples of Rule breakers include </i>Supernatural, <i>the</i> Fallen<i> series, the latter half of the </i>Mortal Instruments<i> series, and many more than I can't be fucked finding.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5149256634598984186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_437725662" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437725662" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11620599-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432185181p2/11620599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437725662?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/11620599-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11620599-sarah?shelf=don-t-recommend">don-t-recommend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437725662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3638350466384847095">This book is everything that is wrong with books. Possibly ever. In the existence of the world. I caught very few usage and spelling errors...so I guess it got that right. Here's what's wrong with the book:<br/><br/>1) The plot. There isn't one. Most books have one of these. This one, for some odd reason, went another way...of meandering endlessly.<br/>2) The main character. Let's see . . . seldom does she actually kick butt, even though, supposedly, she has some sort of super human powers. Waiting on those. S</span>
  <span id="freeText3638350466384847095" style="display:none">This book is everything that is wrong with books. Possibly ever. In the existence of the world. I caught very few usage and spelling errors...so I guess it got that right. Here's what's wrong with the book:<br /><br />1) The plot. There isn't one. Most books have one of these. This one, for some odd reason, went another way...of meandering endlessly.<br />2) The main character. Let's see . . . seldom does she actually kick butt, even though, supposedly, she has some sort of super human powers. Waiting on those. She whines. Endlessly. She's stupid. She's not funny. She's short. She's redheaded (I wouldn't count it against her...but this character deserves more knocks). She's pathetic. Unlikable. Snotty. Stuck up. I could pretty much go on forever.<br />3) The love interest. He's boring. His personality is thus: "I fight bad guys. I love Ellie. I fight bad guys. I love Ellie." It's really not much. I can't even fathom how this nothing personality guy likes her. Not sure which character that reflects worse on.<br />4) The supporting cast. All bad. Snotty, rude friend. Check. Brainy guy. Check. Funny (but not really) guy. Check. Gorgeous girl to be jealous of. Check. Other love interest who is somewhat interesting but makes no sense because he's only in 5 short scenes in the book and spends the whole time saying he's in love (inexplicably) with main girl who he has spent about 5 minutes with, and she cares about him too. Check. Pointless parents. Check.<br />5) The bad guys. They apparently hate executing their evil scheme. They like to give Ellie huge breaks and chunks of time to party and do school and makeout with Will. "Nah," they say, "Let's raise Lillith and Sammael tomorrow. Don't you know Ellie has a bowling party tonight? Too. Important."<br />6) The fight scenes. So abominable that I actually didn't read them. yup. Skipped 'em.<br />7) The parties. Oh. My. Gosh. Let's see...the world is going to become Hell, and all of the humans will be banished to Hell forever...and 80% of this book is parties, school, and Ellie and Will making out.<br /><br />Okay. I have to stop. I could go on forever. The book was so bad. Don't even glance at it in passing. I'm pretty sure that more people reading this book is a scarier apocalypse than the whole Hell on Earth situation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3638350466384847095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_337504620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337504620" />
    <a title="Alexi Silversmith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3449391-alexi-silversmith"><img alt="Alexi Silversmith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272095444p2/3449391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337504620?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexi Silversmith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexi Silversmith" href="/user/show/3449391-alexi-silversmith">Alexi Silversmith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337504620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11740563298676186207">Not even posting the synopsis for this one. It doesn't deserve it. I'm still pissed that GR doesn't offer a minus stars option. Just...WHAT? How does stuff this bad actually get on SHELVES? Is everyone in the publisher on drugs?<br/><br/>Basically, after I ranted to a bunch of my friends about the awful first book in this series (ANGELFIRE) some of them read it too. I ended up feeling much better about the whole thing after we'd all laughed ourselves into hiccuping puddles over how dire it was. So then we</span>
  <span id="freeText11740563298676186207" style="display:none">Not even posting the synopsis for this one. It doesn't deserve it. I'm still pissed that GR doesn't offer a minus stars option. Just...WHAT? How does stuff this bad actually get on SHELVES? Is everyone in the publisher on drugs?<br /><br />Basically, after I ranted to a bunch of my friends about the awful first book in this series (ANGELFIRE) some of them read it too. I ended up feeling much better about the whole thing after we'd all laughed ourselves into hiccuping puddles over how dire it was. So then we decided to give this book a try because, after all, it had to have gotten better, right? Surely everyone concerned would be doing their best to improve on the balls-taped-to-the-cement-and-smashed-with-a-brick HORROR of the first one?<br /><br />Nope. Apparently the horror quotient wasn't high enough yet. I'm convinced at this point that this series is some kind of an experient on the part of HarperCollins. They want to see just how crappy they can go and still get money out of people. It's the only explanation.<br /><br />From the moment (in the first few pages) that Ellie, having been thrown to the ground by a giant Reaper, lies there with her eyes closed for several minutes recapping the previous book while the Reaper that threw her obediantly stands waiting (alert enough to growl, drool and make threats, but not actually bite her head off with its huge motherfreaking teeth) and Ellie's boytoy Will battles with another one unaided, I could see that things had actually managed to get worse. The laughably bad dialogue between Ellie and the Reapers was pretty much a surety after that. Then we get to Ellie's reaction to being grabbed by one of these monstrous beasts that she's supposedly been created to fight. Let's see - you're superstrong and fast, and you have two huge flaming swords, and a mission from heaven to kill Reapers. A Reaper attacks you. What do you do? Well, if you're Ellie:<br /><br />1) Drop swords<br />2) Scream for help<br />3) Allow yourself to be grabbed by the monster's talons<br />4) 'squirm' and 'struggle' helplessly in said talons while said monster flies off with you because it's not like you're some kind of badass that could snap a talon in half, kick this bastard in the face and jump down before it gained altitude or anything<br />5) Scream for help AGAIN<br />6) Get saved and in the process crush your boytoy almost to death<br /><br />Yeah, that's Ellie. She's the one standing between the humans of the world and eternal damnation.<br /><br />WE ARE ALL DOOMED.<br /><br />And the publishing industry is doomed too, if it keeps producing these sort of slimy scrapings as its lead titles. My five year old niece could come up with better shit than this armed only with a sippy cup of juice, the back of a cereal packet and an orange crayon. I'm 100% serious. And I'm 100% done with this crappy ass book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11740563298676186207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer2486030599366824043">When I started reading this book, I was hoping that after her many near-death experiences, Ellie would have grown up, you know, gotten better at prioritizing what's important. For example: saving the world is a heck of a lot more important than partying and having a picture-perfect teen life. But... no, Ellie is every bit as whiny, selfish, annoying, make-me-want-to-rip-my-hair-out as she was in the first book. <br/><br/>I mean, I already hated her when I started, so I assumed that it honestly couldn't ge</span>
  <span id="freeText2486030599366824043" style="display:none">When I started reading this book, I was hoping that after her many near-death experiences, Ellie would have grown up, you know, gotten better at prioritizing what's important. For example: saving the world is a heck of a lot more important than partying and having a picture-perfect teen life. But... no, Ellie is every bit as whiny, selfish, annoying, make-me-want-to-rip-my-hair-out as she was in the first book. <br /><br />I mean, I already hated her when I started, so I assumed that it honestly couldn't get much worse, but oh... it does. If I was to make a list of the top-ten things I would never do as the Preliator, especially knowing that I'm an angel on top of that, <b>getting drunk</b> (which impairs judgement and much needed fighting skills) would be at the top of my list. In that list would also include going to movie nights instead of training/ fighting and whining every ten seconds because life isn't fair. <br /><br />Another thing that bugged me was the plot twist with Ellie's dad. Why? Well for the first book I was completely siding with him for the majority of the time. I know, I know, he was horrible to Ellie but from his perspective, she kinda deserved it. Example: Her "awful" dad buys her a 40,000 dollar car (wish my dad was that awful) and she crashes it after having it for like a week. Her grades are sucking and at her birthday party she was drinking (at 17) and crashed through the window. Another thing that hurt poor wittle Ellie's feelings was when he called her a slut on Halloween, although ELlie, when you leave the house looking like this<br /> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.google.com/imgres?q=slutty+nurse+costume&amp;um=1&amp;hl=en&amp;client=safari&amp;sa=N&amp;rls=en&amp;biw=1242&amp;bih=668&amp;tbm=isch&amp;tbnid=eOdZdQd7yUTurM:&amp;imgrefurl=http://ericmcast.blogspot.com/&amp;docid=eN38WZ1Me9hjEM&amp;imgurl=http://i66.photobucket.com/albums/h267/ericmcastillo/private-nurse-costume.jpg&amp;w=432&amp;h=432&amp;ei=mrtWT53_D8S-2AXlvOnlCQ&amp;zoom=1">http://www.google.com/imgres?q=slutty...</a><br />you've gotta be able to withstand the comments. So when ELlie's dad reveals himself to be a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[demon that had already killed her real dad <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And there are more reasons why I didn't quite like this book, but, well, I'm pretty sure you get the picture, <s>and I'm lazy</s>. For a good angel-related book I would recommend the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> series by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3290920.Cynthia_Hand" title="Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Cynthia Hand</a> and for books with an actually badass heroine I would recommend [book; Hunger Games]and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> (starting book 2, because Rose bugs me in book 1). <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_271467671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271467671" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271467671?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=whiny-annoying-blah-heroine">whiny-annoying-blah-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-dick-to-heroine">hero-dick-to-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=tstl-heroine">tstl-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271467671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3785876837095580801"><b>2.5 stars - Some spoilers</b><br/><br/>Ellie is struggling to balance her normal human life with her duties as the archangel Gabriel. She won't give up her school, friends or social life seeing that they are the only things keeping her sane. Ellie and her guardian, Will are trying to stay one step ahead of the demonic reaper, Bastian who wants to unleash hell on Earth. They are also patrolling the streets at night, fighting demons and fighting their feelings for each other. Will is reluctant to have a relatio</span>
  <span id="freeText3785876837095580801" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars - Some spoilers</b><br /><br />Ellie is struggling to balance her normal human life with her duties as the archangel Gabriel. She won't give up her school, friends or social life seeing that they are the only things keeping her sane. Ellie and her guardian, Will are trying to stay one step ahead of the demonic reaper, Bastian who wants to unleash hell on Earth. They are also patrolling the streets at night, fighting demons and fighting their feelings for each other. Will is reluctant to have a relationship with Ellie since finding out she is actually the archangel Gabriel. Meanwhile Ellie is contending with her jealousy as Will's ex lover, Ava - an angelic reaper makes an appearance to help fight the good fight. Caden, the demonic reaper who helped Ellie stop Bastian in Angelfire, is still around and he's quite predictably taken a shine to Ellie. <br />Will is written as being utterly devoted and madly in love with Ellie for the 500 years they've worked together but this is contradicted by having Will's ex lover turn up, not to mention the talk of his previous girlfriends. Will having previous lovers is fine, but to then to write that Will has this epic love and one a kind devotedness to Ellie just makes it seem untrue. <br />Ellie is slightly more tolerable in this installment but she's still weak and needy. She whimpers, screams and cries in every difficult situation. I think it's good when someone fights for their love, but Ellie begs Will over and over to be with her and frankly it was pathetic. <br />Will was annoying, he just kept sending Ellie mixed signals, he said they couldn't be together yet he didn't allow her to move on. There's some suprises when Will finds out about his mother's past and who his father is.<br />Ellie's best friend Kate was a great character - fun, loyal and understanding. Ava, Will's ex lover was also written very well - she was thoughtful, tough and focused. Both Kate and Ava are better characters than Ellie.<br />The love triangle between Will-Ellie-Cadan was unnecessary as Ellie only had eyes for Will and Cadan was already siding with good so his love for Ellie wasn't needed for Cadan to help the good guys. <br />On the plus side there was more action and loss, which kept things entertaining. There is also insight into Ellie's past lives and it's revealed that Ellie has descendants. I'm hoping this will be explored in the next book and that we get to meet Ellie's great-great-great-etc-grandchildren because maybe that would give Ellie's character some gravitas, instead of Ellie just being all about Will and their <i>super-speshul-one-of-a-kind-undying-lovely-love</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3785876837095580801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_334715859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334715859" />
    <a title="Laura Jennings" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5483784-laura-jennings"><img alt="Laura Jennings" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306034772p2/5483784.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334715859?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Jennings" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Jennings" href="/user/show/5483784-laura-jennings">Laura Jennings</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334715859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5722954254246924204">I swear to god, after reading this, I'm convinced there is a conglomerate of authors that all write the exact same story. "Hey! It's a YA book! Feisty female protagonist with super powers/paranormal abilities/angelic strengths/magical abilities. Priorities? Why, the exact same priorities as any regular old girl, of course! She wants to be popular, be liked, have a boyfriend, and get good grades. Why would any of these different abilities affect their priorities? Don't ask stupid questions! Make </span>
  <span id="freeText5722954254246924204" style="display:none">I swear to god, after reading this, I'm convinced there is a conglomerate of authors that all write the exact same story. "Hey! It's a YA book! Feisty female protagonist with super powers/paranormal abilities/angelic strengths/magical abilities. Priorities? Why, the exact same priorities as any regular old girl, of course! She wants to be popular, be liked, have a boyfriend, and get good grades. Why would any of these different abilities affect their priorities? Don't ask stupid questions! Make her clumsy/too cute/too popular/too rich for a character flaw, and don't forget, she has to struggle with something we all know teenagers can never grasp: responsibility!"<br />	600 hundred year old archangel reincarnated into the body of a human girl … and her priorities are parties and boys? Really? And while I'm on the subject, why do people keep using Biblical mythology when we all know none of them are brave enough to bring up the real big bad: Lucifer. Never in a million years, cause that would land you on the banned books list for being controversial. And god forbid you actually challenge status quos or something; it's just fantasy, right? No, Miss Moulton, you'd just rather talk down to your audience the same way beauty product commercials do. "Girls like pink, right? And boys? Put that in there. And don't forget the only viable way a woman solves her problems is like a man. Come on, come on, this is taking all day!"<br />	I really don’t know how much more of this insulting YA I can read. It's like the exact same stories are being churned out over and over, Hollywood-movie style, smoothly marketable with no variation or originality whatsoever. How is this character different from Clary from Mortal Instruments? From Ever from the Immortals series? How about Tory from the Virals series? They're all exactly the same! WHY? Why didn't the author explore some real deep and intimate truths about what being an archangel would do to one's psyche, one's emotional well-being, one's sense of identity, instead of what it would do to one's social life? The point of any storytelling is to tell the truth, and I cannot for one second believe that the responsibility of taking the world's existence on one's shoulders would make you prioritize like Elli did, not when I've seen teenagers shoulder adulthood over something like domestic abuse, something that is comparably mild to the whole freaking world. This story is a joke, written by an author who apparently thought being a lying liar who lies is the same thing as penning a meaningful tale about coming-of-age and responsibility.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5722954254246924204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_233881378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233881378" />
    <a title="Amber I." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3632431-amber-i"><img alt="Amber I." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432490474p2/3632431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233881378?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber I." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber I." href="/user/show/3632431-amber-i">Amber I.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3632431-amber-i?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233881378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13004036977071974765"><br/>Once I started Wings of the Wicked I honestly could not put it down. I was an emotional roller coaster through out so much of this book. Ellie is facing some of the hardest things ever and she has too much at stake. One wrong move could have disastrous effects. It doesn't help being an archangel she only half remembers and having so many human emotions. Ellie sacrifices so much in this book and not everyone comes out of it alive.<br/><br/><br/>I could not put this down. There was just so much going on and neve</span>
  <span id="freeText13004036977071974765" style="display:none"><br />Once I started Wings of the Wicked I honestly could not put it down. I was an emotional roller coaster through out so much of this book. Ellie is facing some of the hardest things ever and she has too much at stake. One wrong move could have disastrous effects. It doesn't help being an archangel she only half remembers and having so many human emotions. Ellie sacrifices so much in this book and not everyone comes out of it alive.<br /><br /><br />I could not put this down. There was just so much going on and never a dull moment. Every page felt so intense. There is the forbidden relationship between Ellie and Will, that both try to fight because if they let their feelings surface it could mean death. There is also the fact that some close to Ellie turn out not to be who she thought they were. There is that small thing to that almost every night monsters are trying to kill her and destroy the earth. And through out everything she has to try to deal with the fact she is Gabriel an archangel reincarnated for thousands of years and she is also just Ellie a human who goes to high school. Ellie learns more about her past lives, we meet some new characters and we lose some too. Oh and the ending... Its not to crazy of a cliffanger but its enough to make you need the next book asap.<br /><br />I really liked Angelfire but I am in love with Wings of the Wicked. This book was just everything I admire in a Ya novel, it had non stop action, a forbidden love, and a brilliant story that kept me glued to each and every page. If you haven't yet go check out Angelfire and then come devour Wings of the Wicked!</span>

<div id="review_108703651" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108703651" />
    <a title="Krys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2798856-krys"><img alt="Krys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329103793p2/2798856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108703651?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krys" href="/user/show/2798856-krys">Krys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=urban-dark-fantasy-paranormal">urban-dark-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=monster-hunting">monster-hunting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=first-person-narrative">first-person-narrative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=demon-themed">demon-themed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=fallen-guardian-angels">fallen-guardian-angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=state-michigan">state-michigan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108703651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17309034449932377936"><br/>Last year I read, and very much enjoyed, Angelfire by local (to me) author Courtney Allison Moulton. I have since been awaiting the sequel, Wings of the Wicked, with much anticipation. I was hoping it would live up to the promise of the first book. I'm very pleased to say that it has.<br/><br/>Since discovering that she is the Preliator, things for Ellie have become very straight forward, and very confusing at the same time. She spends her nights chasing down demonic reapers with her guardian Will, who ha</span>
  <span id="freeText17309034449932377936" style="display:none"><br />Last year I read, and very much enjoyed, Angelfire by local (to me) author Courtney Allison Moulton. I have since been awaiting the sequel, Wings of the Wicked, with much anticipation. I was hoping it would live up to the promise of the first book. I'm very pleased to say that it has.<br /><br />Since discovering that she is the Preliator, things for Ellie have become very straight forward, and very confusing at the same time. She spends her nights chasing down demonic reapers with her guardian Will, who has been at her side for centuries, despite her many reincarnations. Now their relationship is platonic, which is difficult for them both, especially since they have expressed their feelings for one another. But these things must be swept aside - an ancient evil stirs and war is upon them. Will Ellie be able to balance everything and not lose herself, or, worse, her soul?<br /><br />I found the sequel to Angelfire to be better than the first one...almost. I add a caveat because I had one problem with the ending of the book that skewed my enjoyment a touch. For the first 400+ pages the book was absolutely incredible, dark and intense. The plotting was pitch perfect and the character interactions were funny and compelling and sad...and then one big plot point/reveal happened around, oh, 100 pages away from the end and that was where I wanted it to end. But it did not. It kept going and going. I feel that the end after that major point could have had about 50 pages trimmed out and the flow would have been much better, but, as it is, I grew weary. It's a little disappointing, but only in a minor way. I think the book would have been an absolute 5 if it were not for this one small detail.<br /><br />Other than that one gripe, wow. This was a great read. There are a lot of things that happen to Ellie and company that make this book stunning; Ellie particularly. She goes through some major life changing events in this book, as does Will. I was glad to see Moulton broaden the scope of her characters by that much depth. It makes them well rounded interesting individuals to read. Moulton does manage to defeat the dreaded middle-book-sucking scenario, despite my displeasure with the last few chapters. I really did love this book. A lot. The world is wonderful, the mythology is engaging, and the characters will stay in my brain for a while.<br /><br />Also, I'm completely happy that Moulton added a scene in East Lansing. That made my day. Here's hoping for a smidge more in the next book.<br /><br />4.5 out of 5 stars.<br /> <br />- review courtesy of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliopunkkreads.com">www.bibliopunkkreads.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17309034449932377936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_150880529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150880529" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150880529?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150880529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9510616420866405413">Oh… and now what?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346242i/700685.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As you’ve seen from my <a title='Review: Angelfire' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140835980' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfire</a> review, there is something about this story that really grabbed me. Not sure if it is the angel involvement, or the monster killing action set, but I liked the series and I can’t wait for the next book to come out.<br/><br/>Except for the teenage drama (that at some point got to be a bit tiresome), this book was (as well) really entertaining.<br/>There was plenty of action, tons of monsters to fight, many characters to care about and the ending left me speechle</span>
  <span id="freeText9510616420866405413" style="display:none">Oh… and now what?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346242i/700685.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As you’ve seen from my <a title="Review: Angelfire" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140835980" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfire</a> review, there is something about this story that really grabbed me. Not sure if it is the angel involvement, or the monster killing action set, but I liked the series and I can’t wait for the next book to come out.<br><br>Except for the teenage drama (that at some point got to be a bit tiresome), this book was (as well) really entertaining.<br>There was plenty of action, tons of monsters to fight, many characters to care about and the ending left me speechless.. That’s not the way to end it.. How will I be able to wait so long for the resolution?<br><blockquote>Mark me well, for you will lose everything you love most dear before you finally lose your soul.</blockquote><br>CHARACTERS:<br><br><a href="http://hugmeetskiss.deviantart.com/art/Kiss-The-Cook-220539621" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346242i/700686.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><strong>Ellie</strong><br>Is that kind of character that you might like or dislike in an instant. She is quite undecided and naive at times - for example she wants Will when he doesn't want her (..to want him o_O) and she has second thoughts when he is finally decided – and this adds a bit to the unnecessary drama. Still I liked some of their moments (definitely not the one with the ‘caveman’, but others were cute) and when she was in the mood to fight I liked her even more.<br>I think she was tougher through the first book, but after all that happened with her I can understand that she might be a bit shaken and vulnerable.<br>But, there is always a 'but', when she became too whinny and girlish I wanted to yell at her: <em>what’s wrong with you, you need to save the world, who cares about your needs to go to parties and have a ‘normal’ life, you are so NOT ‘normal’ to start!</em><br><blockquote>"Nice to see you again, Preliator."<br>I snarled, pulling on my chains. "I'll say the same to you when you're dead at my feet."</blockquote><br><strong>Will</strong><br>I have a soft spot for him and I understand him - seeing the girl you love die a hundred times, be with that person for a bit and then feel that awful loneliness for almost 20 years (or even more), not knowing if she's coming back after all, searching for her all over the world and trying to protect her at every cost… This can do no good to a person, human or not. Still, he was <em>way too serious</em>.<br>He needed to relax a bit and enjoy life… Too bad that when he decided to do that the ending left us hanging and there was no more time for having fun.<br><blockquote>I need you to trust me. I need you. And I love you. I want you. You know I do. I will never stop doing those things until the day I die for you.</blockquote><br><strong>Cadan</strong><br>..is fun to be around. I'm not sure what role will he play in the next book, but I have a pretty good idea and I am not loving it.<br>Anyways, I liked him in this book, even though I am not convinced about his reasons. All that he did was a bit too much. In these kind of stories good people are good, bad people are just bad, there are no gray shades, so there must be something that I’m missing here.<br><br><strong>The dad factor </strong><br>I saw almost all of them coming - but the truth is that even though the story was a bit predictable, I still did enjoy it. I love to guess when something good is happening, and I like to be surprised when something bad is changing the course of things... So this was all right. The next book might bring us some more surprises and I am eagerly waiting for them all.<br><br><strong>Nathaniel</strong><br>..was cute from the beginning and I still have some questions about him, not sure if I’ll get my answers, but I really cared about him. He is one of those characters that leave an imprint on the others, and I liked all the moments with him.<br><br>All in one, this was a great transition from the fist book to the last one. I hope that you will like it as well :)<br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9510616420866405413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
